British Red Cross Ambulance Team Bombed by Italian Air Force; Attack Three Kilometers from Eritrean Camp Demonstrates Intent; British Government Prepares to Issue Strong Protest 40

Addis Ababa, Special Correspondent Ochana Reports: Yesterday near Gua Lan Town on the Northern Front, an Italian aircraft suddenly bombed a British Red Cross ambulance team, seriously injuring four people. Three of them were reportedly British natives from Kenya. The tent where the doctor was performing surgery was completely destroyed, and three ambulances were also damaged. The British ambulance team was located three kilometers away from the nearest Eritrean military camp. On the same day, the Italian aircraft first bombed Gua Lan Town, killing ten men, two women, and four children. Then, it flew to the British ambulance team's location, flying low and circling nine times before dropping bombs. At the time, three Eritrean soldiers were inside the ambulance team's camp being treated. (Havas dispatch, 5th)

London: The Foreign Office today received a formal report from Mr. Mei Lai, the director of the British ambulance team in Eritrea, regarding the Italian aircraft bombing. It is currently being actively considered. British authorities had notified the Italian government one day earlier that the British ambulance team would move from Tai Xi to Hua Er Di Ya, and then to Zhua Lan. However, they only continued to notify the Italian government after the team had already arrived in Zhua Lan, following yesterday's bombing. It is expected that the British government will issue a strong protest to the Italian government. According to Mr. Mei Lai's report, the team's location was two miles away from the nearest troops in open terrain. The Italian aircraft repeatedly flew low over the team's tents, dropping a total of forty bombs, destroying three hospital tents, including the surgery and disinfection tents, as well as a heavy-duty vehicle. Initial reports indicated that three children from Kenya who were being treated as wounded were also killed, but it is now known that no staff members were killed or injured. The report also stated that all tents had Red Cross markings, and in the center was a flagpole with a large forty-foot square Red Cross flag hoisted on it. There is no doubt that this bombing was intentional. Since the team arrived in Zhua Lan, and previously in A La Ma Tai and Hua Er Di Ya, Italian aircraft had repeatedly flown low over the tents. (Reuters dispatch, 6th)

London: The news that the British Red Cross ambulance team near Gua Lan Town on the Northern Front in Eritrea was bombed by Italian military aircraft yesterday has caused considerable shock in political circles here. It is said that the ambulance team led by British Major Boergena in Hua Er Di Ya City on the Northern Front in Eritrea was bombed by Italian forces on January 16th of this year. Afterward, British Ambassador to Italy, Sir Drummond, immediately received instructions from the government to notify the Italian government of the British Red Cross ambulance team's moving locations at any time to avoid a recurrence of misunderstandings. Foreign Secretary Eden also notified Italian Ambassador to the UK, Grande, to pay close attention and prevent similar incidents from happening again. However, less than two months later, the tragedy has reoccurred. It is generally believed that the Cabinet will engage with the Italian government regarding this bombing incident, but will wait for the formal report from the British Minister to Eritrea before deciding on the attitude to be adopted. (Havas dispatch, 5th)

Rome: An Italian government spokesman today mentioned the "unfortunate incident" of Italian aircraft bombing the British ambulance team's tents near Gua Lan in Eritrea, saying that the Italian military believed the British ambulance team was still in Tai Xi. The British Embassy only notified the Italian authorities today that it had moved to Gua Lan. Regarding this matter, the British government has not yet issued a protest to the Italian government. The Italian aircraft dropped a total of forty bombs with great force, killing seven patients, but no staff members were harmed. The tents were clearly marked with a forty-foot Red Cross flag. According to the Italian side's description of the bombing, the day before, Italian aircraft were fired upon while flying low to inspect the tents, so they decided to bomb them with explosives the next day. When the bombs fell, thick black smoke rose from the ground, leading the Italian military to believe that ammunition was stored in the tents. (Reuters dispatch, 5th)

Addis Ababa: After the Italian aircraft bombed the British ambulance team near Zhua Lan, British Army Major Bogeon, was killed by an Italian aircraft's bomb on the Northern Front. The major was a lawyer by profession and had previously served in the Third Dragon Guard and the Fourth Royal Irish Rifle Regiment. He was currently working as a transport officer for the British Red Cross team in Eritrea in an honorary capacity. He unfortunately died while retreating with General Gaza's troops from Amba Alarago to Zhua Lan. He arrived in Addis Ababa in early November last year and joined the service of the King of Eritrea, who ordered him to lead the Red Cross team with one hundred mules and ordered them to go to Tai Xi. He was sixty-two years old but still physically strong and had walked three hundred miles from Addis Ababa to Tai Xi. He had participated in the South African and European campaigns. (Reuters dispatch, 6th)

French and American Representatives Agree on Warship Plan; Hai De to Begin Drafting Soon; British-Russian Talks to Begin in Days 45

London: The final stage of the naval conference is progressing rapidly. French and American representatives have agreed on a warship plan today, so the drafting committee can immediately begin work. This plan stipulates warships of 15,000 tons with 14-inch guns, but specifies that if this plan is not signed by the signatories to the Washington Treaty by the end of this year, then the gun caliber will still be changed to 16 inches. Therefore, the gun caliber will depend on whether Japan agrees to sign. British Naval Minister Monsell is currently discussing alternative clauses with the American Chief Representative Davis. The British Naval Minister argues that the agreement should be invalid if the following situations occur: a war occurs, the signatory countries violate the agreement, or non-signatory countries exceed the limits of the agreement. Davis advocates for more specific clauses. This issue is currently being discussed. At the same time, British-German talks are now underway and are promising. Furthermore, British Foreign Secretary Eden has now returned from Geneva, so British-Russian talks are expected to begin in days. (Reuters dispatch, 6th)

London: The General Committee Experts Group of the Naval Conference met this afternoon and first passed the report submitted by the drafting committee regarding qualitative restrictions on various warships (excluding battleships). Then, they studied the problem of "Non-Building Zone" (i.e., stipulating that warships cannot be built between two tonnage figures). It was decided in principle that warships cannot be built between 8,000 tons and 17,500 tons. The tonnage of Class A cruisers was originally set at 10,000 tons, but the Naval Conference has now agreed that construction of this class of cruisers cannot begin in the next eight years. Therefore, the tonnage of Class B cruisers, which is 8,000 tons, is the highest tonnage for cruisers. As for 17,500 tons, it is the lowest tonnage for battleships. The Experts Group then discussed the "Tonnage Flexibility Limit," because after each ship is built, its actual tonnage will inevitably differ slightly from the planned tonnage. If the actual tonnage is less, it will not be a problem, but if it is more, it must be restricted. This limit is set at 100 tons. For example, after a 7,000-ton cruiser is completed, its tonnage cannot exceed 7,100 tons. Finally, the experts studied the following issue: the problem of the displacement of various warships increasing with age according to the laws of physics. It is said that a solution has been found for this. The Experts Group will continue to meet tomorrow to discuss the maximum limits for battleship tonnage and gun caliber. (Havas dispatch, 5th)

Japan's Policy Towards Russia Will Not Be Affected by Coup; Japanese Ambassador Declares to Litvinov 57

Prime Minister Narrowly Escapes Assassination Attempt in Yugoslav Parliament; Opponent Fires Four Shots Unsuccessfully, Assailant Arrested on the Spot 60

Belgrade: The Lower House of Yugoslavia convened at 11:20 this morning to discuss the government budget and foreign policy. Prime Minister and Foreign Minister Stojadinović gave a lengthy speech, praising the policies of Prince Paul, during which all members rose to their feet. At that moment, opposition party member Alauković suddenly fired four shots at Prime Minister Stojadinović. The Prime Minister quickly hid behind the speaker's podium, thus escaping harm. Several members then rushed forward to seize the pistol, several of whom were injured. The assailant was immediately apprehended. It was found that the assailant had brought a pistol to the parliamentary session, sneaking into the gallery. He was also intoxicated and repeatedly interrupted the members' speeches, leading to his removal. He then sat at the far left and seized the opportunity to assassinate the Prime Minister. After this disturbance, the assembly reconvened at 12:40, with Stojadinović safely in attendance. All members, including opposition members, cheered and paid tribute to him. (6th Havas dispatch)

Details of the Suppression of a Heretical Sect in Southern Shandong; The Inside Story of the "Paiqian Dao" Resembles the Communist Party; Investigation Reveals This to Be the Second Group in Shandong 84

Jinan Correspondence: The counties of Zouteng, Mengfeng, etc., in southern Shandong are characterized by overlapping mountains, inconvenient transportation, and a strong-willed populace. Furthermore, bordering northern Jiangsu, the area has long been known as a region difficult to govern due to the prevalence of bandits. It once produced notorious bandit leaders such as Liu Hei Qi (i.e., Liu Guitang), Zhang Hei Lian (already executed in Jinan), and Sun Meiyao and Sun Meizhu. There were also associations such as the Huangsha, Hongqi, and Heiqi. Fortunately, all of these have become a thing of the past due to the provincial authorities' combined efforts of suppression and pacification. Recently, the "Paiqian Dao," also known as the "Yiguan Dao," emerged again in Xicang Village, Teng County. When officials attempted to persuade them to disband, they resisted arrest with knives, injuring police officers. Fortunately, they were quickly suppressed before they could cause major harm. As for its internal workings, it indeed has an effect, resembling communism. It has many followers. The sect was introduced from Jiangsu. The Xicang Paiqian Dao is the second group in Shandong. Its leaders, Wang Shoujin and others, have been arrested and imprisoned in the Teng County Jail. The acting county magistrate, Wang, has come to Jinan to report the details of the situation to the chairman of the provincial government, Han Fuqu, and to request instructions on how to handle the aftermath. The rumor that descendants of Sun Meiyao were inciting rebellion is a misunderstanding of this incident. The details of its beginning and end are recorded below:

The Paiqian Dao, also known as the Yiguan Dao, has been spreading in southern Shandong for a long time, reportedly for over a year. All those who join the sect must hand over all of their personal property to the sect. After this, the individual no longer has any say in the management and disposal of the property. This sect was introduced from Jiangsu several years ago. The leaders of the Paiqian Dao in Xicang Village, Teng County, are two brothers, Wang Shoujin and Wang Shouyin. Initially, they simply set up altars to teach disciples and provide medical treatment, so many ignorant villagers followed them. Currently, there are many believers in the southeast villages, and many Buddhist halls have been established. The sect members hold their meetings at night in secluded places. Outsiders cannot learn about its internal secrets. This arrest was made because the captured criminals confessed, revealing that its internal workings do indeed have an effect, and its behavior is quite similar to that of the Communist Party. The disciples of Xicang Village are the second group in Shandong Province, numbering several hundred. The mark carried by sect members is a red silk symbol with a large red seal. Recently, the sect (during the first month of the lunar calendar) suddenly forged hundreds of steel knives near Yangzhuang Village near Xicang Village. Villagers were shocked and informed each other, knowing that they had ulterior motives.

Xie Xiweng, the County Magistrate of Teng County, is currently in Beijing for training, and Wang is acting as county magistrate. After receiving a confidential report, he immediately dispatched Director Ma of the Public Security Bureau, accompanied by several followers, to the village on the morning of the first of this month to persuade the leaders to disband immediately and return to farming. He also wanted to take Wang Shoujin, Wang Shouyin, and others to the county seat. Director Ma first went to Lincheng, met with Inspector Ma, and led twenty armed police officers to Xicang Village to persuade the sect members and announce the county magistrate's order. However, they not only ignored the warnings but also gathered dozens of sect members, wielding knives and resorting to violence. Seeing the unfavorable situation, Director Ma immediately escaped over the wall. His accompanying police officers were cut and injured. After escaping, Ma reported to Battalion Commander Kong of the Lincheng garrison and requested reinforcements to rescue the surrounded police officers. After receiving the report, Battalion Commander Kong dispatched two companies of soldiers and went to the rescue with Director Ma. After arriving in the village, Battalion Commander Kong first sent Platoon Leader Wang with six soldiers into the village for a final warning. Unexpectedly, the sect members, upon seeing the government troops, attacked them with knives before they could even speak. Platoon Leader Wang defended himself with a pistol, fighting as he retreated. The sect members, relying on their heretical arts, disregarded the law and cut down several soldiers, pursuing them out of the village. Seeing that persuasion was impossible, the main force of government troops attacked with platoon fire. However, the sect members were in high spirits and chased the government troops half a li away. After a long stalemate, the sect members' heretical arts failed, and they were completely defeated. Platoon Leader Wang and the besieged police officers were rescued. In this battle, three soldiers were killed and five were seriously injured. On the second day, they were all sent to the Huabei Hospital in Teng County for treatment. At noon on the second day, a meeting was held in the county government to discuss the aftermath. That evening, the captured criminals and suspects, twenty-seven in total, were escorted to the county government, along with a list of sect members, which included hundreds of people. Acting County Magistrate Wang reported to Han in Jinan that evening and returned to Teng County on the 4th. (4th)

Guangdong Province Prohibits Gold Exports, Limiting the Export Quota to 200 Yuan Worth of Gold; Provincial Bank Formulates Regulations for Purchasing Pure Gold 85

Guangzhou Correspondence: Since the currency reform in Guangdong Province, legal tender has been in circulation. At the same time, provincial and municipal banks have been buying silver and fractional currency from various locations, which has been steadily concentrated in Guangzhou. According to a report from the Provincial Bank, it has collected more than 50 million yuan of silver and continues to buy it. It has also begun to buy gold, announcing that people should bring gold to the Provincial Bank to sell. The Provincial Bank has formulated regulations for purchasing gold to facilitate people's requests to sell. The regulations are as follows: In order to collect gold, the bank has specially formulated purchase regulations. Merchants and people may bring their stored gold to the bank for purchase at any time. Gold shall be limited to gold leaves and gold bars. The minimum weight for each delivery shall be 25 taels. The price will be announced daily by the bank. After the bank collects gold, it must be refined and tested to determine the fineness. A refining fee of one yuan per tael of gold shall be charged. The standard gold fineness shall be 99%. If the fineness is too low, and the test results show that it is less than 99%, the seller shall pay a smelting fee of one yuan per tael of gold. After the bank tests and accepts the gold delivered by merchants and people, it will first issue a receipt. After the test is completed, the price will be given according to the fineness. However, if the seller has a substantial shop guarantee or is jointly guaranteed by several shops, and the bank approves it, it may issue a portion of the value in advance at the time of purchase. The final settlement will be made based on the fineness after the test. If there are any changes to the regulations, they will be announced separately.

While the authorities are buying gold, they are strictly prohibiting the export of gold leaves and gold bars to prevent the outflow of gold. Anyone carrying gold jewelry for export must not exceed 200 yuan in value. If this amount is exceeded, the excess gold will be confiscated and treated as smuggling. The temporary regulations on the prohibition of gold exports were formulated by the Department of Finance yesterday and submitted to the Provincial Government for promulgation and implementation on the first of this month. The Customs Superintendents of all customs offices were also ordered to comply with the regulations. The five items of the Temporary Regulations on the Prohibition of Gold Exports in Guangdong Province are attached below. Article 1: These regulations are based on Article 3 of the Measures for the Prohibition of Gold Exports issued by the Ministry of Finance, which sets the export limit at 500 yuan in national currency. This is considered too high and, given the situation in this province, there is a risk of gold outflow, so special regulations are made. The other two articles still follow the Ministry's regulations. (Note: Article 1 of the Ministry of Finance's Measures for the Prohibition of Gold Exports states that the term "gold jewelry" refers to items whose shape or part is made of gold. Article 2 states that the gold jewelry carried by travelers must be for their own personal use only.) Article 2: The total value of gold jewelry carried by travelers must not exceed 200 yuan of legal currency in this province. Article 3: If the gold jewelry carried by travelers exceeds the limit in the preceding article, the excess portion may be confiscated. Article 4: Anyone who stores gold jewelry or gold leaves and gold bars, as well as ornaments containing gold, may go to the Guangdong Provincial Bank and its branches to have them purchased by the bank at the price of pure gold announced by the Provincial Bank. Article 5: These regulations shall be submitted by the Provincial Government to the Political Affairs Committee for approval and promulgation. (March 2)

Anhui Disaster Relief Association Distributes Funds for Drought and Bandit Disasters; A Total of 55,000 Yuan 86

Anqing Correspondence: The Anhui Provincial Disaster Relief Association, considering the counties that suffered from drought and bandit disasters last year, and facing the current spring famine, with frost and snow exceeding the severity of winter, the starving people are in urgent need of relief. In addition to the counties in northern Anhui that have already received funds, Shou County and Huoqiu County are the most severely affected by the drought and have each been allocated an additional 3,000 yuan, totaling 6,000 yuan. The following is a list of allocated funds for the counties in central and southern Anhui: Drought disaster: Fuyang, Linquan, Xuyi, Tianchang, Quanjiao, and Hefei counties each receive 3,000 yuan; Hao County, Jiashan, Chuxian, and Lai'an counties each receive 2,000 yuan; Lihuang and Lujiang counties each receive 1,500 yuan, totaling 29,000 yuan. Bandit disaster: Jing County receives 2,000 yuan, plus an additional 1,000 yuan; Dongliu, Guichi, Susong, Taihu, Qianshan, Tongcheng, and Huoshan counties each receive 2,000 yuan, totaling 17,000 yuan. An allocation of donations for the relief of children in disaster areas will also be made: Lihuang receives 600 yuan; Shou County and Huoqiu County each receive 250 yuan; Fuyang, Linquan, Xuyi, Tianchang, Quanjiao, Hefei, Hao County, Jiashan, Chuxian, Lai'an, Lujiang, Jing County, Dongliu, Guichi, Susong, Taihu, Qianshan, Tongcheng, and Huoshan counties each receive 100 yuan. The total allocation amounts to 55,000 yuan. It is planned to send personnel to the counties immediately to expedite the investigation and distribution. (March 3)

Songjiang: Verdict Announced in Xiaokunshan Kidnapping Case 87

In the kidnapping case of the grandson of the Fan family in Xiaokunshan, the subordinate county, last October, the Public Security Bureau devised a plan to capture Mao Jinzhang, who was in charge of negotiating the ransom with the victim's family, on the spot. Mao confessed that Zhu Guangyuan was the mastermind and that Sheng Qinghe and Zhu Baokang were accomplices. All three confessed to the Public Security Bureau and wrote their confessions. Since the case was a criminal matter, they were sent to the local court for trial. However, they repeatedly recanted their confessions during the investigation. However, due to the existence of written confessions and solid corroborating evidence, they were sentenced on the 6th. Zhu Guangyuan was sentenced to death for kidnapping and demanding ransom. Sheng Qinghe, Zhu Baokang, and Mao Jinzhang were each sentenced to life imprisonment. It is reported that the defendants all declared their intention to appeal upon hearing the verdict.

Wang Gong has been appointed as the Administrative Supervisory Commissioner and Security Commander of the Songjiang District. Wang sent Yang Mengchu and others to Songjiang the other day. Accompanied by the county government, they selected the former site of the People's Education Hall as the location for the office. Preparations are currently underway. It is reported that Commissioner Wang will arrive in Songjiang around the 10th to take office.

Suzhou: Deng Banghai Scheduled to Take Office 89

Since Deng Banghai was announced as the new County Magistrate of Wu County by the province, the former incumbent, Wu Qiyun, has repeatedly telegraphed him to come to Suzhou to take over the seal of office so that he can relinquish his post as soon as possible. Changshu: Three or Four Clerks Resign from County Government 90

After the new County Magistrate Chen Fu took office on the first day, the clerks of various departments have not yet been announced. Although the original incumbents still come to the office every day, they are very uneasy. New personnel are arriving one after another and being placed in various departments. On the 5th, Pang Shoubai, the head of the Third Department, resigned because the Third Department handles construction affairs and the clerks are all specialized. Now, new people are being inserted, and it is impossible to know whether they can handle affairs effectively. If mistakes are discovered in the future, the department head cannot be held responsible. Therefore, he applied for resignation. The technicians in his department also resigned one after another. Geng Boyang, the head of the Fourth Department, and other clerks also expressed their intention to resign, and Geng has already left Changshu on the 6th.

Wuxi: Constructing Lakeside Scenic Forest 91

The county's afforestation movement, according to the implementation measures stipulated in the county government's afforestation plan for the 24th year, is to create a lakeside scenic forest. It is planned to start this year with the creation of pure forests of Masson pine, maple, zelkova, ginkgo, locust, bamboo, crowdipper, chinaberry, mulberry, and other species. The surrounding area is estimated to be 250 mu, with the lakeside foothills of the third and fourth districts as the implementation sites. Shen Xichun, a technician from the Provincial Sericulture Experiment Station, has been commissioned as the afforestation specialist to conduct surveys in the area. It has been determined to open an orchard in Dayaowan in the fourth district. There are more than 100 mu of barren hills there, and it is planned to plant various fruit trees. However, the mountain is Qin clan public land of Dahe, and more than 80 mu pay grain. Huazang Mountain is suitable for opening a pine garden with more than 1,000 mu of mountain land for planting trees. As the Arbor Day on March 12th is approaching, the county government is actively preparing to complete the work by the end of March to embellish the lakeside scenery.

Increasing Opium Retail and Smoking Locations, Expanding Opium Addiction Treatment Centers 92

After the county government was ordered to carry out the self-renewal registration of opium addicts, the number of opium addicts increased sharply. The original retail and smoking locations were insufficient, so it ordered all district public offices to conduct thorough investigations and appropriately increase the number of locations. Yesterday, it was learned that the various districts reported that there were seventy or eighty locations applying for increases. Fang Guoding, the head of the Third Department, went to the countryside to inspect and formulated measures for increasing the number of retail and smoking locations, divided into A, B, and C grades. Grade A is allowed to set up eight lamps and accommodate sixty opium smokers. Grade B is allowed six lamps and accommodate forty people. Grade C is allowed four lamps and accommodate twenty people. In addition, the county's opium addiction treatment center can only accommodate 120 opium addicts per round. According to the provincial order to ban opium addiction within four years, it is necessary to expand the center. Therefore, it was decided to actively expand the center to accommodate more opium addicts and ban opium addiction as scheduled.

Changzhou: Villagers Robbed and Looted Late at Night 93

Liu Hanting, a farmer from Donggang Township, Third District of Wuyi County, is over sixty years old and has a well-to-do family. At about 2 a.m. on the 3rd, more than twenty bandits suddenly came, holding box guns and flashlights, jumped over the surrounding wall, tied up Liu Hanting and hung him from the beams to beat him, asking where he hid his money. They overturned boxes and chests, looting all the clothes and ornaments, and opened the iron safe. All the deeds and more than 800 silver dollars were also looted.

Homicide Case Solved, Criminal Arrested 94

Lu Fengsheng of Zhengping Township, Sixth District of Wuyi County, was recently secretly reported to the county government by his son for privately possessing firearms and doing evil. The county government ordered a detective team to go to the countryside for two decisive investigations before arresting him and bringing him to the county. During interrogation on the night of the 4th, Lu Fengsheng refused to admit involvement in robbery, only admitting to theft in two cases. Regarding firearms, he said that they were deposited in his home by a local vendor, Su Guofang. After detailed interrogation, he admitted that he had watched a play in Heqiao the previous year with Jiang Xiaolong and four others. On the way, due to jealousy and adultery, he and the other two used ropes to strangle Jiang Xiaolong to death and sink him into the river near Wudong Bridge. As the crime was serious, he was ordered to be sent to the local court's prosecutor's office for interrogation.

Nantong: Sandbar Breaks Up Human Trafficking Ring 95

Recently, human traffickers have been rampant in the counties under Nantong's jurisdiction. Those who are lured and abducted are all young women, who are fornicated with guests and then sold to Shanghai, Wuxi and other places as prostitutes. Many people have been victimized. Later, the Public Security Bureau broke up a human trafficking ring in Shazhou, arresting more than a dozen male and female human traffickers and rescuing many abducted girls. The human traffickers Wang Bingfang and Gao Gui Guniang were sentenced to four years of imprisonment each after being tried by the court on the 5th.

Turnover of Administrative Personnel in Tongyi 96

Ge Tan, the special commissioner of the Nantong District, arrived in Nantong from Shanghai on the 5th to take office, and appointed Li Xiangcheng as the department head and Wu Jingxiu as the director of the district management office. Jin Zonghua, the county magistrate of Nantong County, was transferred to the county magistrate of Xinghua County. His successor is Hong Sheng, the secretary of the Wuxi Special Office. Hong will arrive in Tong on the 10th to take office. In addition, Zhang Yi, the captain of the 16th Security Brigade, came to Tong on the 5th to take office.

Yangzhou: Order to Clearly Delineate Military and Civilian Land 97

The military properties in various places in Yangzhou City, such as Yuanmen Bridge, Jiaochang Street, east and west barracks, etc., were previously reported for land registration and compliance with regulations, resulting in the suspicion of repeated payment of land tax. The property owners submitted a request to the county government to be forwarded to the department for instructions and explanations. The county government has now received instructions from the Finance Department, which roughly stated that if the households have been paying military rent in accordance with regulations, they can be exempted from land tax. However, the amount of military land must be delineated from the civilian land and counted separately. On the 3rd, County Magistrate Ma instructed the relevant First District Public Office to start the investigation and report to the county for verification and forwarding.

Intercepting Opium and Injuring People, Arrest and Prosecution 98

Lu Jinxian, a resident of Jiusheng Township, Third District of Jiangdu, learned of the whereabouts of the well-known opium dealer Shu Fanggui. He gathered many people, hoping to intercept and seize the opium he was carrying. As expected, in the afternoon of the previous day, he encountered Shu carrying dozens of taels of opium passing through the area. During the struggle, Shu Fanggui's head was beaten and injured by Lu, and he was bleeding profusely. Seeing that he had caused injury, Lu arrested Shu, together with dozens of taels of opium, and reported to the township public office, which reported to the Toutouqiao Security Third Detachment stationed there. The detachment sent a team to escort them to the Li Dianzhen Detachment Headquarters for investigation. On the 4th, the detachment sent the prisoners and opium to the county government for disposition.

Gaoyou: Public Organizations Telegraph for Rural Relief 99

Ding Fengnian, a standing committee member of the county party headquarters; Wang Bangping, the executive chairman of the Anti-Smoking Committee; Wang Hongzao, the chairman of the Chamber of Commerce; Yu Hui, the chief of staff of the Farmers' Association; and gentry such as Ma Junqing and Dong Zhongxin, considering that since the breach of the Min-20 dyke, the rural economy has been extremely bankrupt. The Farmers' Bank of Jiangsu Province has branches in various counties and towns to provide rural relief, but this county has not yet established a branch. They have repeatedly appealed, but to no avail. As the spring famine approaches, farmers are in urgent need of loans. They recently telegraphed Zhao Dihua, the Director of the Jiangsu Finance Department and the Manager of the Provincial Farmers' Bank, requesting that a branch be established in You as soon as possible to provide relief.

Yangqing Road Will Soon Resume Traffic 100

The Yangqing long-distance bus service was suspended after the Su-Zi No. 1208 vehicle overturned into the canal outside Fengshen Temple in the northern gate of Youjing on the afternoon of January 6 this year, drowning eight passengers, including Li Zhengshu, creating an unprecedented tragedy. The Construction Department is preparing for improvements. Regarding the local improvement issues, the road will be straightened by cutting bends, widening the road surface, and paving the slopes. The estimated total cost is more than 20,000 yuan, and work is underway. All the original vehicles on the line have been transported to the province. The Highway Administration is currently working overtime to rush the construction, striving to reduce the size of the body and reduce the capacity by one-third to avoid danger. It is expected that the repairs will be completed in early next month, and normal traffic can be resumed around mid-month.

Ningbo: Yuyao Salt Farmers Starving to Death 101

The salt farmers in Yuyao field have been suffering unspeakable hardships because the collection of salt has been stopped for half a year. On the 4th of this month, salt farmer Ma Guangshun and his two daughters of Xiamajia Road starved to death because their food supply was exhausted. In addition, the cattle of four salt farmer families in Hujia Road also starved to death one after another because they had no money to buy food. According to local residents, if there is no relief measure within a few days, the future of the salt farmers will be unimaginable.

Resignation of the Head of Zhenhai People's Education Center Approved 102

Xu Deyang, the head of the Zhenhai County People's Education Center, has served for five years and has achieved remarkable results. Xu recently resigned to the Provincial Education Department because of the difficulty of handling affairs. After hearing the news, all sectors of Zhenyi telegraphed to retain him. The Education Department approved Xu's resignation because he was determined to resign. Liu Youshu has been appointed to fill the vacancy.

Travel Notes from Hankou to Guangzhou (II) 103

— Zhao Junhao

(Travel Communication by Our Reporter) From Hankou to Changsha

The Jihe Wheel arrived in Hankou at 8:00 a.m. on the 2nd. We first went to the Jiangbian Hostel of the China Travel Agency for a short rest. The weather in Hankou was extremely cold, and the cold wind was biting. At about 10:00 a.m., Mr. Hu Xuantang of the Wuchang Transportation Office of the Yuehan Railway Zhushao Section entertained us to go to Wuchang. We crossed the river by the Hubei Construction Department ferry and landed at Hanyang Gate. We immediately climbed the Yellow Crane Tower to look around. The Yellow Crane Tower is no longer the original building, but a newly built tall Western-style building. The so-called Yellow Crane Tower of the past can only be glimpsed in the window of a photography studio. Looking out from the Yellow Crane Tower, Hankou and Hanyang are clearly visible, and the sails rising and falling in the Yangtze River are magnificent. The strategic importance of the three towns of Wuhan can be seen from the Yellow Crane Tower. After the tour, we took a rickshaw along the river bank to Xujiapeng, which is the starting station of the Yuehan Railway Wuchang-Changsha Section (i.e., Xiang-E Road), and the material transportation office of the Zhushao Section is also located there. I originally thought that the scale of the Xiang-E Road was not very large, but when I was there, I found that the scope of the Xiang-E Road Administration was no less than that of the Jinpu and Pinghan lines. All kinds of equipment were available, and there were dozens of office buildings and staff residences. However, the damage to the vehicles and the bumps in the ride on this road are probably unmatched by any other road in the country. We had to wait for the train to Changsha to depart at 8:30 p.m., and it was no use waiting in Xujiapeng, so we returned to Hankou to spend half a day. The streets of Hankou are clean and tidy, and the buildings in the French Concession are beautiful, but the market is very depressed, and the purchasing power of the residents is very weak. Even the Central Grand Theater, which is known as "the best in sound and light, and famous in the three towns of Wuhan," is very desolate. We went to see the "Three Stars Shining on the Moon" starring the Marx Brothers, and there were only a dozen spectators. Such a good film in such a large theater, but the business is so sluggish, this alone can illustrate the rest.

At 6:00 p.m., we took the Yuehan Railway ferry across the river and returned to Xujiapeng in Wuchang. Ten minutes later, we arrived. When the entire Yuehan Railway is open to traffic, Xujiapeng will become more important. In the future, if we handle joint transportation with various Yangtze River lines, and passengers and goods first arrive in Hankou and then cross the river to here, there will be many detours. I think we should speed up the construction of wharves in Xujiapeng to meet the needs. If the Shanghai-Hankou ships first call at Xujiapeng and then go to Hankou, it will be appropriate. The state-run China Merchants Steam Navigation Company should take action immediately. After we arrived in Xujiapeng, we boarded the Xiang-E Road train to Changsha. Xujiapeng Station is very small, even smaller than Xujiahui Station on the Shanghai-Hangzhou-Ningbo Railway. Although there are electric lights on the station, they are dim and the situation is bleak. That night, there were only three first-class rooms, each with four berths, so those who were traveling with female relatives had to hesitate. If there were many first-class passengers at the same time, men and women had to share a room, which was very inconvenient. We enjoyed the convenience of pre-booked berths in Shanghai, but here it was completely ruined. The electric lights in the first-class room were also very dim, and there were no quilts. We had to pay the porter to rent them. Three days ago, from Shanghai to Beijing, the lights on the train were bright and the blankets were as white as snow. Compared with this, there was a world of difference. I am not aiming at enjoyment, but that passengers should receive the corresponding treatment for the corresponding fare. From Wuchang to Changsha is only 365 kilometers, and the first-class fare is more than 14 yuan. The train started at 8:30 p.m., and the severe shaking made people's hearts break. Passengers in the carriage were like babies sleeping in a cradle. The degree of vibration affected every part of the body. That night, I lay in the car, drowsy, half asleep, half awake; the painful situation is difficult to describe. At dawn, I got up and sat up, trying to calm myself, and looked at the scenery outside the car, hoping that Changsha would finally arrive. I have studied the reasons why the Xiang-E Road has deteriorated to this point, and there are also reasons for this. Since there is a waterway from Hubei to Hunan, and the time is not very long, those who travel between Hunan and Hubei are trying to save money and take small wheels, which are economical and comfortable. Therefore, the railway business is sluggish, and the income is small, and the road maintenance costs are naturally unavailable. Therefore, the sleepers are rotten and cannot be replaced, and the vehicles are dilapidated and cannot be purchased, and they are left to fall into a state of no return. Now that the entire Yuehan Road is about to be open to traffic, the Xiang-E Road authorities are hoping that the entire road will be open to traffic, and they are also trying to reorganize it. If they can thoroughly reform, then those who travel on the road in the future can avoid the suffering of sitting in a cradle!

The largest station on the way from Hubei to Hunan is Yuezhou, but unfortunately, we passed through it in the dark, and I was sorry that I could not see Dongting. In the morning, we passed Miluo Station and saw the clear Miluo River. The water was shallow and the sand was bright, and the scenery was beautiful. From Miluo onwards, the sky was bright, and the scenery on both sides was fully visible. The fields in Hunan Province are all terraced, with deep water and thick soil, which is known to be fertile. Old trees are connected to the mountains, and the fences are interspersed, with a general view of paddy fields and shady summer trees. The mountains seen along the way are mostly ochre-red, and at the end of the mountains there must be large plains, because Hunan Province is completely a basin. At 10:40 a.m., we arrived in Changsha. Mr. Zhong Shusheng, the director of the Zhuzhou Material Factory of the Zhushao Section, Mr. Wang Yinqing, the director of the Wuchang Transportation Office, and Mr. Wu Yaoshu of the China Travel Agency met us at the station. The beauty and order of Changsha surprised us. The streets are mostly paved with large stone slabs, which are more neat than Suzhou and Hangzhou. In the prosperous areas, the scale of the shops is almost the same as that of Shanghai. Changsha is also vigorously carrying out the New Life Movement. Magnetic signs of "Pedestrians walk on the left and keep order" can be seen everywhere on the road. After careful inspection, I saw that pedestrians on the street walked on the left, and those who came walked on the right, without any slack. I occasionally did not pay attention and smoked in the middle of the road, and was also dissuaded by the police. Changsha has a unique phenomenon, that is, young soldiers can be seen everywhere, and it is not known which troops they belong to. This situation seems to be unique to other places. Xiang embroidery is sold in the city, and it can be found everywhere, but the prices are expensive and not fine products. We crossed the waters of the land continent (such as the Huxin Pavilion in West Lake) and crossed the Xiang River twice to visit Yuelu Mountain. At the foot of the mountain, Yuelu Academy is one of the four major academies where Zhu Zi lectured. It is now Hunan University, with a grand scale and elegant environment. It is a good place for study. There is a couplet hanging outside the school gate, which reads "Only Chu has talents" and "Here is the prosperity". From the top of Yuelu Mountain, you can overlook Changsha and have a panoramic view. The Xiang River reflects the sails back and forth, which is extremely spectacular. That night, we stayed in Changsha, and will go to Zhuzhou Lukou tomorrow (4th). (Sent from Changsha on March 3)

Draft Amendment to the Publications Law to be Submitted to the Next Central Political Conference for Review 104

The draft amendment to the Publications Law has been reviewed and approved by the relevant departments of the Executive Yuan after the Central Political Conference re-established the principles and submitted it for amendment. It was submitted to the Executive Yuan meeting for discussion on the 2nd. It is understood that it will be sent to the Central Political Conference for review. The full text consists of seven chapters and fifty-seven articles. The main contents of the amendment are: The source of funds and the income and expenditure budget have been changed to the amount of capital and the economic situation. The item of editing and publishing plan has been deleted. When a newspaper or magazine is detained, the local government should report to the superior government for approval before it can be executed. The advertisement published in the newspaper is regarded as the author of the person who requested the publication. If the publication contains content that harms good customs or violates criminal law, in addition to being handled by those who have the right to prosecute according to law, the local police station may, based on the complaint of the person concerned, give the person in charge of the publication a warning or a fine. The original draft has been revised a lot. The summary of the revised draft is as follows:

Chapter 1 General Provisions

Article 1. Publications in this law refer to documents and pictures printed by mechanical printing plates or chemical methods for sale or distribution.

Article 2. Publications are divided into the following three types: 1. Newspapers refer to those that are published under a fixed name daily or at intervals of no more than six days; 2. Magazines refer to those that are published under a fixed name weekly or at intervals of no more than three months; however, if the content mainly publishes current events, it is still regarded as a newspaper; 3. Books and other publications refer to all publications other than the first two categories. Extra editions or supplements of newspapers or magazines are regarded as newspapers or magazines.

Article 3. The publisher in this law refers to the person who hosts the publication.

Article 4 The author in this law refers to the person who writes documents and draws pictures. The person who takes notes of other people's speeches and publishes them in publications or asks others to publish them is regarded as the author, but if the speaker agrees, he shall bear the same responsibility as the author. Regarding the compilation of works, the compiler is regarded as the author, but if the original author agrees, he shall bear the same responsibility as the author. Regarding the translation of works, the translator is regarded as the author. Regarding publications written in the name of specialized schools, companies, associations or other organizations, the representative of the school, company, association or other organization is regarded as the author. The advertisement published in the newspaper is regarded as the author of the person who requested the publication. If the person who requested the publication is unknown or has no ability to bear civil liability, the publisher is regarded as the author.

Article 5. The editor in this law refers to the person who is in charge of editing the newspaper or magazine.

Article 6. The local competent authority in this law is the county government or the municipal government in the province, and the social affairs bureau in the city that is subordinate to the Executive Yuan.

Chapter 2 Newspapers and Magazines

Article 8. To publish a newspaper or magazine, the publisher shall fill out a registration application and submit it to the local competent authority where the publishing office is located before the first publication, and the local competent authority shall forward it to the provincial government or the municipal government that is subordinate to the Executive Yuan for approval within 15 days before it can be published. The provincial government or the municipal government that is subordinate to the Executive Yuan shall approve the registration application in the preceding paragraph within 28 days after receiving it, except in special circumstances, and forward it to the Ministry of the Interior for issuing a registration certificate. After issuing the registration certificate, the Ministry of the Interior shall send a copy of the registration application to the Central Propaganda Department. The registration application shall state the following items: 1. The name of the newspaper or magazine; 2. The organization of the newspaper office; 3. The amount of capital and the economic situation. Those who publish newspapers shall also state the amount of the guarantee money; 4. The frequency of publication. Those who publish newspapers shall also state the number of pages; (Note: Items 3 and 4 are amended) 5. The name and location of the publishing office and the printing office; 6. The name, age, experience and residence of the publisher and the editor.

Article 9. Those who apply for registration for publishing a newspaper shall submit a guarantee money to the local competent authority. The amount of the guarantee money and the method of submitting and returning it shall be determined by the Ministry of the Interior. (Note: This article is newly added) Article 13. The editor of a newspaper shall not be appointed until he has been registered. The preceding paragraph shall be determined by another ordinance. (Note: Both of the above articles are newly added)

Chapter 4 Matters to be Published in Publications

Article 23. Publications shall not contain the following records: 1. Those who intend to undermine the Three People's Principles of the Chinese Kuomintang; 2. Those who intend to subvert the National Government or harm the interests of the Republic of China; 3. Those who intend to disrupt public order. Article 23. Publications shall not contain records that harm good customs. Article 24. Publications shall not publish debates on cases prohibited from public litigation. Regarding litigation cases, no criticism shall be made until after the judgment. Article 25. In wartime or in the event of disturbances or other special necessities, military and political organs may report to the National Government to prohibit or restrict the publication of matters relating to politics, military affairs, diplomacy or local security.

Chapter 5 Administrative Sanctions

Article 29. If the Ministry of the Interior considers that the publication contains one of the matters listed in Article 22, or violates the prohibitions or restrictions stipulated in Article 25, it may specify the matter and prohibit the sale and distribution of the publication, and may detain it when necessary. The publication detained in accordance with the preceding paragraph may be returned upon the request of the publisher when the record of the matter is deleted or the prohibition is lifted. If the circumstances stipulated in the first paragraph are minor, the local competent authority may submit it to the provincial or municipal government for approval and give a warning, and the provincial or municipal government shall forward it to the Ministry of the Interior. Article 30. If the local competent authority finds a publication in the first paragraph of the preceding article, if it considers it necessary, it may temporarily prohibit the sale and distribution of the publication, or temporarily detain it, and at the same time submit it to the provincial government or the municipal government that is subordinate to the Executive Yuan for forwarding to the Ministry of the Interior for approval. Article 33. If the circumstances of the punishment stipulated in paragraph 1 of Article 29 are serious due to the matters published in the newspaper or magazine, the Ministry of the Interior may suspend the publication of the newspaper or magazine for a fixed period or permanently. If a newspaper or magazine that violates the prohibition in the preceding paragraph is published, the local competent authority shall detain it. Article 34. When detaining books or other publications, it is necessary to detain the original plates. Article 35. If the publication contains provisions that violate Article 23 or violate criminal law, in addition to being handled by those who have the right to prosecute according to law, the police authority in charge may, based on its authority or the complaint of the person concerned, give the publisher of the publication a warning or a fine of not more than one hundred yuan.

Chapter 6 Penal Provisions

Article 45. Those who violate the provisions of Article 22 shall be sentenced to imprisonment for a term of not more than one year, detention, or a fine of not more than one thousand yuan to the publisher, editor, author, and printer, but if other laws provide for a heavier punishment (according to its provisions, Article 47. Those who violate the prohibitions or restrictions stipulated in Article 25 shall be sentenced to imprisonment for a term of not more than one year, detention, or a fine of not more than one thousand yuan to the publisher, editor, author, and printer. Article 51. A publisher who violates the prohibition stipulated in Article 29 shall be sentenced to imprisonment for a term of not more than one year, detention, or a fine of not more than one thousand yuan. Anyone who knowingly sells or distributes the publication shall be sentenced to imprisonment for a term of not more than six months, detention, or a fine of not more than five hundred yuan. Article 33. A publisher who violates the prohibition in paragraph 1 of Article 33 shall be sentenced to imprisonment for a term of not more than one year, detention, or a fine of not more than one thousand yuan. Anyone who knowingly sells or distributes the newspaper or magazine shall be sentenced to imprisonment for a term of not more than six months, detention, or a fine of not more than five hundred yuan. Article 54. The provisions of the Criminal Law on habitual offenders and concurrent punishments shall not apply to the crimes stipulated in this law. Article 55. The right to prosecute for the crimes stipulated in this law shall be extinguished by prescription if it is not exercised for more than one year. The limitation period for the right to prosecute for the crimes in Article 45 and Article 47 shall be calculated from the date of publication.

Local News

New Appointed Ambassador to Japan, Xu Shiying, Departed Yesterday for His Post; Boarded Ship Last Night and Set Sail at Midnight This Morning; Mayor Wu Hosted a Tea Party to Bid Farewell Before Departure 105

Our newly appointed ambassador to Japan, Mr. Xu Shiying, along with his staff, departed last night on the Japanese ship Asama Maru to take up his new post in Japan. Before his departure, he telegraphed Ding Shaoyi, the chargé d'affaires at the embassy in Japan, to inform him of his itinerary. Shanghai Mayor Wu Tiecheng held a special tea party before Mr. Xu's departure to bid him farewell. The details are recorded below, along with a conversation with Japan.

Conversation with Japan

Ambassador Xu, at 11:00 AM yesterday, responded to an invitation from the Japanese Tokyo Nichi Nichi Shimbun newspaper and spoke with a representative of the newspaper via international wireless telephone. The representative first inquired about Mr. Xu's confirmed date of arrival and then requested Mr. Xu to express his aspirations for accepting the mission to Japan and his opinions on future Sino-Japanese diplomacy. Ambassador Xu answered each question in detail. The conversation lasted for more than ten minutes. As he was about to leave the country, Mr. Xu could not continue to serve as the chairman of the Guanghua Petroleum Company and sent a letter to the company's board of directors to resign.

Mayor's Tea Party

In addition to arranging all the matters for his departure, Mr. Xu also bid farewell to the retired army veteran Duan Zhigui, who was living in Shanghai, and other parties. Shanghai Mayor Wu Tiecheng held a grand tea party at his private residence on Haig Road from 5:00 PM to 7:00 PM last night to bid him farewell. Those invited to accompany him included Zhou Yu, the director of the Ministry of Foreign Affairs' Shanghai office, Yu Hongjun, the secretary-general of the municipal government, the directors of various bureaus of the municipal government, and over a hundred leaders from various sectors.

Departure Last Night

After attending Mayor Wu's tea party, Mr. Xu returned to his private residence for a short rest. Then, at 11:20 PM, accompanied by his secretary Huang Ruixuan, he went directly to the Huishan Wharf in Yangshupu and boarded the Japanese ship Asama Maru. Those who went to the wharf to bid him farewell included Guo You'an, representing Duan Qirui; Li Dachao, representing Mayor Wu; Zhou Yu, director of the Ministry of Foreign Affairs' Shanghai office; Zhao Tiezhang, deputy director; Cai Jingjun, director of the Municipal Public Security Bureau; Wang Zhinan, representing Yang Hu, the director of the Security Department; Wang Simo, the president of the Second Special District Court; and Qian Xinzhi, Xu Xinliu, Wen Lanting, Du Yuesheng, Zhang Xiaolin, Zhao Jinqing, Zhu Qinglan, Xu Xiuzhi, Liu Yunfang, as well as Ashino, the intelligence chief of the Japanese Embassy; Ishii, the consul general in Shanghai; Funatsu, the Japanese director of the Public Works Department; and representatives from the Huangshan Construction Committee and the Renji Hall, totaling over a hundred people. Mr. Xu immediately met with reporters from various newspapers on the ship. According to his answers to the reporters' questions, he said, "Having been ordered to serve as ambassador to Japan, I will abide by the government's orders and do my best to promote the improvement of Sino-Japanese relations, so as to live up to the expectations of the entire country." Afterwards, they bid farewell one after another. The ship set sail from Shanghai at midnight.

Telegram Announcing Departure

After deciding on his departure date, Mr. Xu telegraphed Ding Shaoyi, the chargé d'affaires at the embassy in Japan, on the evening of the 5th to inform him of his itinerary. The Asama Maru will arrive in Kobe on the 9th and will not transfer elsewhere. He will then take a train directly to Tokyo to take up his post. The embassy staff accompanying Mr. Xu include Counselor Wang Pengsheng, Secretaries Huang Ruixuan and Hu Mai, and a retinue of five people. Mr. Xu's private secretary, Lin Xiaogu, went to Japan last week to make all the arrangements.

Carrying Local Products

Upon deciding to go to Japan to take up his post, Mr. Xu purchased a large quantity of famous domestic products, such as Jiangxi porcelain, Anhui brushes and ink, and Xuan paper, in preparation for bringing them to his post and distributing them to Japanese officials and friends in Japan. In addition, he purchased thirty small bottles of Shaoxing aged wine to bring to his post to be used for banquets.

Reason for Changing Ships

It is reported that Mr. Xu originally planned to take the Dollar Steamship Company's President Hoover on the 3rd of this month to take up his post. However, the departure date was suddenly postponed. According to a reporter from the New Sound News Agency, the reason for Mr. Xu's postponement was due to the recruitment by the shipping company. When Mr. Xu intended to take the Hoover, the Dollar Steamship Company expressed goodwill and was willing to fly the ambassador's flag for Mr. Xu to show its respect. When the matter was heard by the Nippon Yusen Kaisha, they sent personnel to request Mr. Xu to take a Japanese ship, as it was appropriate for the ambassador to Japan to take a Japanese ship during this time of Sino-Japanese friendship. They also promised an 80% discount on tickets and other items, and also agreed to fly the ambassador's flag to show their respect. Therefore, Mr. Xu, considering the sincerity of the Japanese shipping company, postponed his departure and changed to a Japanese ship.

The Mint's February Production: Factory-Made Subsidiary Coins; Approved for Release, Announcement to the Public 106

Announcement by the Central Mint Examination Committee (No. 31): For the purpose of announcement, upon investigation, the Class B 1,000-yuan factory bars (880 fineness) produced by the Central Mint in February of the 25th year, from No. 56294 to No. 56381, a total of 88 bars, have been stamped by Inspector Ge Laide, who was appointed by the committee, in accordance with the regulations. The fineness and weight of each bar have been listed and registered. In addition, the new subsidiary coins produced by the factory in the same month include 890,000 20-cent nickel coins, 2.7 million 10-cent nickel coins, 4.68 million 5-cent nickel coins, 25.5 million 1-cent copper coins, and 8.52 million half-cent copper coins. All five types of subsidiary coins have been sealed under the supervision of personnel sent by the committee. In addition to being approved for release separately, a detailed table is attached for public notice. This announcement is made by Chairman Kong Xiangxi, Republic of China, March 2, 25th year.

Large Batch of New Subsidiary Coins Shipped to Beijing; Transferred to Xuzhou, Jinan, and Qingdao for Circulation; Three Batches Totaling Over 23,000 107

Since the Ministry of Finance issued new subsidiary coins, they have been used uniformly in various places, and the exchange is extremely crowded. Although the Central Mint has added night shifts to speed up production, it still feels insufficient for circulation. For the sake of needs in Xuzhou, Jinan, Qingdao, and other places, a large batch of new subsidiary coins has been shipped to Beijing in recent days, and then transferred by the Central Bank of Nanjing to the Xuzhou, Jinan, and Qingdao branches for circulation. The first batch was 12,800 yuan, the second batch was 6,000 yuan, and the third batch was 5,000 yuan. They were shipped to Beijing on the China Merchants Steam Navigation Company's Jiang'an ship a few days ago. The three batches totaled 23,800 yuan. The Central Mint is still continuing to add night shifts to meet the needs of various places.

Jiangxi Yumin Bank Transports Goods for Customers; Transported from the Zhejiang-Jiangxi Railway and Shanghai-Hangzhou-Ningbo Railway to Shanghai 108

In order to facilitate people's livelihood and develop agricultural, industrial, and commercial enterprises, the Jiangxi Yumin Bank has established branches and offices in various counties of western Jiangxi and other places in recent years, and has established special transportation departments in places where various steamships converge to engage in the transfer and transportation of import and export goods for customers. Jiangxi exports include rice, porcelain, tea, summer cloth, and paper, while imports include cotton yarn, piece goods, flour, hardware, and miscellaneous foreign goods. It is said that rice exports are the largest, with a huge annual volume of hundreds of thousands of bags. Since the bank established an office in Shanghai, its transfer and transportation of import and export goods for customers has become even more developed. However, before the Zhejiang-Jiangxi Railway was extended to Nanchang, Jiangxi, a small number of these transports were still entrusted to foreign shipping companies for shipping on the Yangtze River. In order to seek faster and more convenient transport, it has now been changed to transport via the Zhejiang-Jiangxi Railway, through the Shanghai-Hangzhou-Ningbo Railway. The bank has negotiated with the Traffic Department of the two railway bureaus and has been allowed to report and transport goods for customers (limited to goods imported and exported from Jiangxi) and given special treatment, exempting it from all deposits. The Beijing-Shanghai and Shanghai-Hangzhou-Ningbo Railway Bureaus believe that the matter is related to the development of the interior and is also beneficial to the business of the railway, and have agreed to a one-year trial. However, in order to prevent merchants from citing this as a precedent, they have instructed the bank to submit a letter of certification from the主管官廳主管官廳 (responsible authorities) in order to emphasize the intention of cooperation and high regard for transportation.

Ministry of Finance Approves the National Goods Factory Association; Detailed Rules for Relief Loans Have Been Established 109

The Shanghai National Goods Factory Association previously requested the Ministry of Finance to allocate 20 million yuan of Reconstruction Public Bonds to relieve industry and commerce due to the economic downturn. Yesterday, the Ministry of Finance replied: "Your petition of February 13, 25th year, requesting the approval to allocate 20 million yuan of Reconstruction Public Bonds to the Bank of China and the Bank of Communications for exclusive management of chattel and real estate mortgage loans for national goods factories in order to maintain the national goods industry and the livelihood of all workers, has been noted. The Ministry has always attached great importance to the relief of industry and commerce. Last year, the Shanghai Industry and Commerce Loan Review Committee was established to handle industry and commerce loans, and the Ministry allocated 20 million yuan of treasury bills as the second guarantee for the loans, and stipulated ten principles for the relief of Shanghai's industry and commerce loans. Article 2 clearly stipulates that loan applications for industry and commerce are limited to factories that manufacture national goods, merchants that sell national goods, and those that transport national goods for export. The Loan Committee has been ordered to comply with the regulations and instructed the Shanghai Bankers Association and the Chamber of Commerce to file the case. If the factories of the association do need loan relief, they should directly negotiate and handle the matter in accordance with the loan rules approved by the Loan Committee."

Siamese Commercial Envoy Talks About the Situation of Overseas Chinese in Siam; Emphatically States That the Siamese Government Does Not Mistreat Overseas Chinese 110

According to the Shenshi News Agency, Siamese Commercial Envoy Ao Chetanata, since arriving in China on Tuesday (the 3rd), has gone to Beijing to meet with our foreign affairs, railway, and other authorities to discuss increasing Sino-Siamese trade and plans to establish a commercial office in Shanghai to communicate Sino-Siamese commercial information. After completing his official duties, he will return to Shanghai on the evening of the 3rd and is scheduled to take a ship to Hong Kong on the 10th of this month to return to Siam. Then, in May or June, he will first come to Shanghai to establish the special office. According to Ao's statement to the Chinese and Western press corps, reports of the Siamese government mistreating overseas Chinese are not as severe as reported. Here is a brief record of his key points:

Overseas Chinese and Siamese Citizens Receive Equal Treatment

A large number of overseas Chinese reside in Siam, most of whom are engaged in the rice industry. Although there is no formal trade agreement between China and Siam, the Siamese government treats overseas Chinese merchants and citizens scattered throughout the country equally with local Siamese citizens and does not discriminate against them. Even the private interactions between Siamese citizens and overseas Chinese are very affectionate, and there is absolutely no mistreatment or animosity. The rumors that the Siamese government mistreats overseas Chinese are unbelievable.

Educational Situation of Overseas Chinese in Siam

Ao went on to describe the Siamese government's implementation of compulsory education regulations, etc. This matter was already in place fifteen years ago and is not solely implemented on overseas Chinese children; Siamese citizens are also subject to the same treatment. It is not unusual for overseas Chinese children to attend school to learn Siamese. Private schools run by overseas Chinese in Siam have come to Nanjing, Beiping, and various cultural regions to conduct on-the-ground investigations of China's education and culture to learn from them. At present, the textbooks used in private schools run by overseas Chinese are also compiled by education inspection specialists. Therefore, whether Siamese or overseas Chinese children attend school, the situation is equivalent to studying in China. However, more than ten private schools run by overseas Chinese were ordered to be closed because they were found to be suspicious.

Overseas Chinese Are Absolutely Free to Go to Siam

The rumors that overseas Chinese who are raised in Siam cannot return to their country at will are also absolutely false. Overseas Chinese in Siam can return to their country at any time or return to Siam to reside. Overseas Chinese who have a definite address in Siam and are recorded by the Siamese government do not need to pay fees for import and export. According to Siamese import regulations, there are also no special restrictions on overseas Chinese. Chinese people who travel or investigate in Siam can stay in the country for free for three months. However, those who exceed the limit or reside for a long time must pay 100 Siamese coins per year, which is equivalent to 140 Chinese coins.

Trade Situation of Overseas Chinese in Siam

There are no fewer than one million overseas Chinese in Siam. In addition to most of them being engaged in the rice industry and farming, others are engaged in the national goods industry. Therefore, the transportation and sale of national goods in the Siamese market is still controlled by overseas Chinese. The annual business volume is also quite considerable. In addition, the potential power of overseas Chinese engaged in the rubber and aquatic vegetable industries in Siam cannot be underestimated. The Siamese government also gives overseas Chinese freedom to set up real estate in Siam without restrictions.

Poor Weather Between Guizhou and Yunnan; Kunming Aircraft Forced to Land; Aircraft Dispatched Yesterday to Search Have Not Yet Found the Landing Site 111

The China National Aviation Corporation's Chongqing-Kunming Qian San three-engine Kunming Ford aircraft flew from Chongqing to Guiyang at 12:15 noon on the 5th of this month. It arrived in Guiyang at 2:15 PM on the afternoon of the same day. It refueled in Guiyang and left Guiyang at 2:50 PM, originally planning to fly back to Chongqing. At 3:30 PM, it received a wireless telegram from the aircraft stating that the aircraft had flown near Tongzi at that time. At 4:10 PM, it was reported that the weather ahead was extremely bad and it could not proceed, so it had to turn back to Guiyang. At 5:05 PM, it was reported that the weather in Guiyang had also suddenly changed for the worse, so it could not fly to Guiyang either. At 5:50 PM, the pilot reported that the aircraft was covered in ice and snow. The pilot decided that the weather was good at the time, so he raised the aircraft above the clouds and decided to proceed to Kunming. Until 6:25 PM, the aircraft reported that it was still above the clouds and flying towards the Yunnan border. At 6:30 PM, it was reported that the aircraft would land in Qujing, Yunnan. Since then, the company has not received any report on the landing situation. It is questionable whether the wireless machine was damaged by the shock after the aircraft landed. The company has been deeply concerned that the Kunming station has not reported the aircraft's arrival in Kunming since 7:00 PM on the afternoon of the 5th. On the 6th (yesterday), it received a telegram from the Fei Yang office stating that Director Gu had dispatched a military aircraft to search for the aircraft's whereabouts. However, according to the latest telegram, the military aircraft returned to Anshun due to poor weather. Therefore, as of 6:00 PM last night, the company had not received any definite news about the aircraft's landing. The Kunming three-engine aircraft was carrying three passengers, pilot O'Harai, co-pilot Tan Boqi, and wireless operator Chen Naian. The company also sent a telegram to the Kunming station yesterday ordering personnel to take cars along the land route to search for the aircraft in the Qujing area, but it has not received any reply on the outcome.

The Tongshang Steamer Ran Aground on Shiyezhou Beach 115

The Stern Faces the Sky and the Bow Faces Down, a Dangerous Situation; No Hope of Escape During This Shallow Water Period

The Tongshang steamer of the Tongshang Steamship Company ran aground on Shiyezhou Beach due to the river pilot's mistaken navigation on the Yangtze River. At that time, it was unknown what happened, but the stern was high on the beach, and the bottom of the ship had no water scale, while the bow was still on the shallow beach by the river, with only a little more than a foot of river water, resulting in a high stern and low bow. It is very dangerous. The stern cabin is suspended on the shore because the ship ran aground first, and then tried to free itself and turn the ship, resulting in the current situation. There is no hope of escape during this one or two months of shallow water. After receiving the news, the Shanghai company provided food to the crew, but there was no way to rescue it.

Hunan Steamer Departs for Tianjin Today 116

The First Ship After Navigation in the North Sea

From the beginning of January to today, for more than sixty days, the sea off Dagukou has been blocked by ice. A total of more than forty ships have been stranded in Shanghai and Tianjin, and the goods piled up in the warehouses in both places. No Chinese merchant ships in Shanghai dared to sail to Tianjin. Now that the ice is gradually melting and the sea route is open, the Taikoo Company's Hunan steamer has decided to sail as usual because the ship's hull has not been damaged. Fully loaded with passengers and goods, it will depart from Shanghai for Tianjin today. This is the first ship from Shanghai to Tianjin after the ice blocked Dagukou. The Ewo Steamship Company's Fuxing steamer, also fully loaded with passengers and goods, will follow the Hunan steamer.

Antiquities Exhibited in England Will Be Shipped Back; Ye Gongchuo's Opinion 117

Foreigners Participating in the Display of Our Country's Antiquities Is a Great Shame to Our Country's History

The Chinese Antiquities Exhibition held in London has been attracting a large number of visitors since it opened at the end of November last year. Westerners who appreciate our country's art have praised it in unison. However, the exhibition closed on the 3rd of this month, and the exhibited antiquities will be shipped back to China in the middle of next month. According to Ye Gongchuo, a member of the Antiquities Preservation Committee, the Chinese antiquities exhibited in London will be shipped directly to Beijing after they are shipped back next month, and will be unloaded in Beijing. After being publicly exhibited in Beijing, they will be sent to the Antiquities Preservation Library for preservation. However, the impression given to Westerners by the Chinese antiquities exhibited in England this time, although praised by Westerners for the art itself, is a great shame to our country on the other hand. The antiquities that our country transported to England for display are only a part of them. Other countries such as England, the United States, Japan, and France all have our country's antiquities participating in the exhibition. This is enough to show the stain on our country's history. The Chinese antiquities obtained by foreigners were mostly taken away when the Sino-French Allied Forces and the Eight-Nation Alliance attacked Beijing during the wars of the Former Qing Dynasty. In addition, there were many unscrupulous Chinese who coveted heavy profits and privately sold national antiquities to foreigners. These antiquities were all displayed at the exhibition by foreigners, which we feel is a great shame.

Ministry of Industry Supports the Shanghai International Exposition; Guo Bingwen, Director of the International Trade Bureau, Gives a Speech 118

Various matters for the Shanghai International Exposition (i.e., the Shanghai World Exposition reported in the previous newspaper), which is being actively prepared to be held in Shanghai, are being carried out separately. The construction of the venue can be completed in June, and it will officially open on July 1. The Ministry of Industry and leaders from all walks of life in Shanghai, both Chinese and foreign, believe that the holding of the exposition in Shanghai is sufficient to save the decline of the city's market and have expressed their support. Guo Bingwen, Director of the International Trade Bureau, gave a special speech on this yesterday. In addition to expressing his support, he also hoped that the national goods industry throughout the country would send their fine products to the exhibition at that time so that the people of the country would have a deep understanding of purchasing and using national goods. The details of Guo's speech and the recent progress of the exhibition are recorded as follows:

Guo's Speech

According to Guo Bingwen, Director of the International Trade Bureau, to a reporter from the Central News Agency, the depression of our country's industry and commerce is partly due to the lack of purchasing power of the people and partly due to the psychology of the middle and upper classes who love to use foreign goods. For example, in cosmetics and clothing, there are fine national goods, but annual imports still account for a large figure. After repeated national goods exhibitions, this psychology has gradually changed slightly. Now that Chinese and foreign people are preparing for the Shanghai International Exposition in Shanghai and will gather Chinese and foreign goods for public exhibition at the venue, on the one hand, consumers can know that there are indeed national goods that rival foreign goods, and on the other hand, manufacturers can know how to improve by observing and comparing. At the same time, foreign audiences can also have a considerable understanding of excellent Chinese goods and know what to purchase. Therefore, if the exhibition is handled properly and the products displayed by the manufacturers are carefully selected, it will be helpful to the future of revitalizing national goods.

Display of National Goods

The venue of the exhibition, at the intersection of Yangshupu Road and Guangxin Road, has already started construction and can be completed in mid-June. It will officially open on July 1. As for all the preparatory matters, according to news from the preparatory office of the exhibition at No. 356 Jing'an Temple Road, the equipment in the venue is divided into two parts: exposition and entertainment. The entertainment part will concentrate various mechanical and artistic entertainment in one place to enhance the interest of visitors. The exposition part, in addition to setting up a special national goods display department and a national goods retail department to promote national goods, will also collect and display various Chinese and foreign cultural and artistic goods in categories for the public to view. In recent days, many national goods manufacturers have heard the news and have come to request to participate. Because there are many famous local products and valuable items in various provinces and cities of our country, letters have been sent to the agencies in various provinces, cities, and border areas to invite them to select excellent items and transport them to the exhibition for the public to observe.
