Shen Bao Local Supplement

Talk

More Than Three Hundred Ferrymen Cause Disturbance 238

— Da Mu

I once saw a foreign film featuring a mechanically constructed human body that could perform all human tasks, efficiently and quickly, without fatigue, hunger, clothing, or illness, producing more and consuming less. At the time, I was delighted at the prospect of such robots working in the world and even hoped they could come to China.

Material scientific civilization in the 20th century has already reached a critical point, and it is not difficult to imagine a situation where all human affairs are mechanized. However, once that situation is realized, the question of whether people left idle can eat or obtain a livelihood becomes a major problem. This is evident even in the current social situation. This "evident" aspect is particularly pronounced in China.

According to reports: "At Dongjiadu in the Southern District... on the first day of operating the ferry... more than three hundred former ferrymen gathered at the docks on both the east and west banks... Their momentum was fierce. The dock manager, seeing the situation, feared that an incident would occur and immediately opened the iron gate... The Municipal Public Security Bureau dispatched an additional... seventy police officers to persuade the ferrymen to disperse..." and so on.

To the average person, this may seem like an insignificant disturbance. In reality, ferries are faster and safer than small boats, which is "convenient for travelers." This convenience, of course, relies on machinery. However, let us think about those "more than three hundred former ferrymen." The work they depended on for a living has been completely taken away by one or two machines. How will they support their families in the future? They have no place left to sell their strength and sweat, and they are forced to watch the omnipotent machines flaunt their power before them. Their disturbance is nothing less than a plea to society: to demand the restoration of their lost jobs, to demand the continuation of their lives.

As people living in this century, we do not oppose science, material progress, and the improvement and needs of machinery. However, distorted development is probably not beneficial for society. Capitalists originally wanted to use machinery to increase productivity and seize vast wealth; but on the other hand, they also have to find a way out for the millions of unemployed people squeezed out of the circle of life. "More than three hundred ferrymen causing disturbance" is just the beginning. "Persuading them to disperse" is, after all, only a temporary measure, isn't it?

The mechanical human body in the movie makes me shiver a bit.

In the Carriage 239

— Zhuo Er

"Don't even mention it! Ever since—" He glanced at that Greater Empire citizen, "ever since... the occupation of Guandong, there hasn't been a single day of peace. It's as if everything belongs to them. Aren't they holding the knife handle in their hands? What's there to say? What's there to say..."

"Perfectly good people are being arrested for no reason and might be shot at any moment. They call them 'bandits' or 'outlaws.' Where is justice? Really," (he lowered his voice) "it's the righteous army fighting them to the death that they can't handle..."

"Why did you come south?"

"I couldn't stay there any longer. I really couldn't stand it. We just can't bear the injustice! There's simply no justice... alas..." He couldn't go on!

"Is escaping the solution?" I asked him again.

"Well, it's still better than being a subjugated slave, isn't it?" he continued, his tone now resolute and forceful! "This, as long as we have breath, we'll settle the score later..."

He said hatefully, as if forgetting himself and everyone else. He recalled his experiences and poured them out endlessly. Undoubtedly, an indelible record had already formed in his mind. Let his record deepen! Deepen! When it can't deepen any further, let it erupt! Truly... let it erupt uncontrollably... let it be replaced by a bloody, glorious, and clear record!

After that, he fell silent! His face was expressionless, and he sank into thought!

The train stopped at Hangzhou Station. The incomprehensible hawking voices from outside the station still filled my ears! At that time, that citizen from the friendly nation had already left the station, still wearing that stiff-faced, self-important, and arrogant expression! His face was still raised, desperately raised—raised to the sky, until he disappeared into the crowd. (The End)

Copying Old Articles 240

— Zi Nan

There are many rats in my house. It's alright during the day, but at night it's practically a rat world. They even fight on top of the mosquito net.

I wake up in the middle of the night to the sound of rats gnawing at the broken box under the bed. I worry about that box of old books. The next morning, I open it up and, as expected, a box of old books has turned into half a box. The ones that haven't been shredded are riddled with holes and covered in urine and feces. The rats have impolitely taken up residence as their mansion.

I have a habit when organizing books! I read them as I organize them, which means it always takes me half a day. This time is no exception.

As I flipped through them, I came across a tattered copy of "Sanxian Ji". Because the top few pages had been soiled with urine, I tore them off and threw them away, so what was left started from page fifty-one. On page fifty-one was an article called "Describing Hong Kong's Congratulations on Christmas". At first, I thought it was about the so-called "foreign winter solstice" "Christmas" because the words "Christmas" were followed by "Hong Kong". But then I saw that it was actually about "The Birthday of the Great Accomplished Sage and Teacher Confucius". So I patted my slightly smelly hands and continued reading—

The article "described" "literary figures and scholars improvising with their brushes", "described" various schools "performing new plays or showing movies at night" after the Christmas ceremony. It also "described" the "new-style couplets" at the school gates and the "speeches expressing congratulations on Confucius' birthday" in the newspapers. It also "described" the "Licentious Empress" produced by the "Confucius Sacred Society," as well as "Ji Gong's Biography", "Havoc in Heaven", and "Wu Song Kills His Sister-in-Law" being performed in other theaters.

After reading it, I smiled slightly and set it aside. When I had finished sorting and was about to wrap the books in newspapers and tie them up with string, I suddenly froze. It turned out that the

newspaper actually had a "Beijing dispatch" about "Christmas".

They:

Qian (Male) School Gate Couplet

Based on the history of Lu, writing the Spring and Autumn Annals, condemning Tian Heng of Qi, the principle is righteous and the way of heaven is right, overthrowing treacherous sons and rebellious ministers, avoiding red propaganda, demanding revenge for the father's hatred, communism and public wives, destroying moral principles and ethics.

Slaying the Three Du, emerging from Cangjia, executing Shaozheng Mao, the wind acts swiftly and the thunder is fierce, eradicating corrupt officials and tyrannical clerks, training youth in moral education, cultivating oneself and managing the family, loving parents and respecting elders, saving the world and the hearts of the people.

Kun (Female) School Gate Couplet

The mother relies on the son's nobility, the wife relies on the husband's honor, now is the time to sincerely celebrate the sacred, it is appropriate to revere the three obediences, how can you speak of freedom, shut your mouths and submit, blindly misunderstanding freedom, following the trend and becoming fickle.

Men receive Qian's strength, women occupy Kun's compliance, at this moment we respect the principles of Confucius, do not violate the four virtues, don't say what is what, what is what, until you don't know what is what, following society and showing off.

The original book has an explanation for the latter couplet: "Mai" means to close, "you" means what, "you" means none. It is because women and petty people do not know elegant teachings, so vulgar words are used.

Lamp 242

— Liang Qijun

I love lamps.

At night, hiding in my small room, quietly, I put away the books I'm tired of reading. I only feel that there is nothing else as lovely as this pale blue light.

In the notes or novels of my predecessors, I often read about young widows and nuns who are devoted to asceticism, accompanied by green lamps, spending their lives lonely and desolate. If, on a quiet autumn night, you hear the paulownia trees outside telling their sorrows in the night wind, and you happen to read these stories, you might shed tears of sympathy. However, I don't love lamps for this reason.

Because—

Under its gentle comfort, everyone feels that light is great and eternal. – We should thank the lamp, the only "messenger of light" in the dark night.

(Have you ever seen the small grass growing in a dark place? How pitiful it is! Weak, pale.

(...Without light, it's like having no life.)

Because of the lamp, I think of the moth. I watch the little thing constantly circling the lamp, flying and dancing with all its might. Clever people will reveal contemptuous sneers and say,

— A foolish thing.

However, who is foolish and who is clever?

The most clever are often the most foolish.

Novel

Early Winter in Qingyang Port (11) 243

— Qiu Yuan

It was already past mid-morning, and the sun was shining. Qiuhua was tidying her disheveled hair.

— We still have to go to one place, to Jiading, to Suzhou, to Kunshan?

— No, let's go to Qingyang Port. We've never been there before. Have you been there before?

— No, good, let's go together.

— I'm afraid it's too late now, we won't make the train.

— Well, let's see.

She hurriedly tidied her clothes, stepped onto a rickshaw, and arrived at the train station at five minutes before nine. She bought a ticket and ran onto the platform. The stationmaster had already prepared the red and green flags. The carriages were crowded with people. They walked and walked until they reached the foremost third-class carriage, where they found two empty seats. It seemed as if it was a match made in heaven for Zhuo Min and Qiuhua. The train left Zhenru. The scenery of the Jiangnan region in early winter showed no signs of withering. The leaves were always so green, and the fields stretched endlessly, which, although monotonous, also broadened one's horizons; the red maple leaves dotted the plains, making one feel the natural charm of the countryside even more. The sun gently shone in through the train window. People's complexions were so pleasant, and on the soft faces that didn't use any modern cosmetics, there floated a natural, harmonious color reflected from the heart.

Leftover Sound

The Bailu Society, which has been absent from the radio for a long time, has now reorganized and will broadcast on China & West today, led by Mr. Liu Di and Mr. Ma Tinglong.

Miss Bai Shan, a new member of the Bailu Society and a student of music, will broadcast her self-composed song "Picking Lotus Seeds" today. Listeners should be able to tune in at that time. (Mo Hong)

It is said that the Peilei Song and Dance Troupe will perform in major theaters in this city.

It is said that Miss Dong Li, formerly of the Art and Culture Troupe, has joined the Mingyue Society.

Zhou Lei of the Dilei Troupe is currently playing the piano in the Xiayun Song and Dance Troupe of Shanghai World.

It is said that Wang Kai, Ye Ying, and Ye Hong have withdrawn from the Lianyi Society. (Xiao Zhang)

Shanghai Yuanchang Advertising Company's Mimi Collection magazine, published by the radio station, has been in circulation for two years. Now the twelfth issue of the second volume (total number 24) has been published. The content is rich, including ballad singing openings, vignettes, a radio frequency table. This issue also includes sheet music for the Hoeing Dance Song, etc. Each copy is sold for 20 cents, and a full year's subscription of twelve issues is 2.2 yuan. Postage is an additional 10%. The general distributor is No. 7 Sanrangfang, Caishi Road, Shanghai. The Shanghai South general sales office is the "Lidu" service agency across from the Minli Girls' Middle School, Wenmiao Road, West Gate, Shanghai.

It is said that the Chongsheng Society will publish the Chongsheng Monthly.

News from the Yiguang Society is silent.

The Chongsheng Society convened its second general meeting of members on March 7 to discuss performances and plans to perform in Ningbo's hometown association and other projects. (Above, Bai Chong)

Film

James Cagney's New Work: "Ceiling Zero" Premieres Today 251

Warner Brothers' latest aviation passion blockbuster, "Ceiling Zero," starring the "daredevil" superstar James Cagney and Pat O'Brien (who will collaborate again in "China Clipper"), is scheduled to premiere today at the Grand Theater. The film is adapted from the Broadway stage hit that ran for six months. It tells the story of a brave and promising young man who sacrifices his life for science. The director is Howard Hawks, renowned in Hollywood for his aviation films. "Hell's Angels" was one of his directorial works. At a time when slogans of national salvation through aviation are shouted everywhere, this film serves as an excellent stimulant. As for James Cagney's acting, he remains true to his past style, portraying a courageous and lively young man.

"Bridal Chamber Night" Premieres in Paris 252

"Bridal Chamber Night" is the film that made Gary Cooper, the lead of "A Farewell to Arms," famous, and is also the first collaboration between him and Anna Sten, the star of "Nana" and "Resurrection." The story revolves around the lack of freedom in women's marriages, a delicate flower ravaged by storms. Beauty has always had a tragic fate. The bridal chamber is like a execution ground, filled with sorrow and lingering emotions. Even a heart of stone would shed tears upon seeing it, and even plants would be moved. May all the sentimental movie fans in the world have the fortune to see it.

Silver Jottings 253

— Zhi Er

"Fa Yang" Bai Nan said: "Film criticism is now in complete decline." (Confucius said: Probably because "Daily Film" has ceased publication.) I wonder if the articles written by Bai Nan in Silhouettes count as "film criticism"?

Tell Mr. "Philosopher" that Wu Han's "service attitude" is "very responsible," arriving early and leaving late. After the six o'clock working hours, he still goes to the director's department to discuss for an hour, very "actively working."

Wu Han's first achievement in Mingxing: From now on, all drafts written by the publicity department will be reviewed by the director's department before publication. (It is said that the position is presided over by the superficial Wang Gong, congratulations!)

"Philosopher" Xu Suling (current "Prime Minister" of Yi Hua) said: "Those who truly bury themselves in hard work will always get what they deserve. Yi Hua Company was ruined in the hands of a large number of amateurs, and the corrupt group also left Yi Hua. Everyone thought Yi Hua was hopeless, with no money, no actors, no future, nothing. But recently, Yi Hua Company has shown signs of revival. Who says there is no hope for Chinese films?" (Confucius said: "To represent one's own words as public opinion - I really don't understand how humans can be so despicable.")

Has Yi Hua been revived? I think it's a little too early to say. But our obligatory advertisement must be made: To the "helpless" film company bosses: Currently, there is "someone who can produce some results and is definitely not an amateur," a "contributor to the revival of Yi Hua," those who want to "revive," why not come! Addendum: The so-called "revival" probably means being able to run to Nanjing.

(Confucius said: What is Xu Suling's "a bit of achievement"? It's "Bridal Chamber Night." To avoid saying "representing one's own words as public opinion," right and wrong should be left to public opinion.)

"Two Brothers" Lead Actress Lu Lixia's Memorial Photograph 254

Young Women's Club Entertainment Gathering 255

With Famous Movie Stars Participating in Performances

The entertainment gathering organized by the Young Women's Club has been fully prepared and is scheduled to be held today (7th) at 2 p.m. at the YMCA on Sichuan Road. In addition to the original music, singing, and dramas, famous movie stars Wang Renmei, Li Lili, Chen Boer, and Lan Ping will personally participate in the performances. The program is diverse and exceptionally exciting. It is said that ticket prices are divided into three types: two yuan, one yuan, and two jiao.

Shanghai Drama Film Research Institute 256

Recruiting Free Students

The Shanghai Drama Film Research Institute, located in Park Lane, Jiangwan Road, in this city, is organized by drama and film celebrities such as Lu Shi. The person in charge of the institute, in view of the current needs of society, in addition to recruiting undergraduates, has specially created a drama and art practice class with free tuition to cultivate practical drama talents and benefit enthusiasts with financial difficulties. It is also heard that after graduation, the students will be able to become basic members of the institute's professional theater troupe. The application period is from now until the 15th of this month. Details are available by mail.
